Oh, sons, I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by the completion of it you will achieve perfection in it, and by its explanations and declarations, it seems to me that I have provided you with a treatment that is part of the operation of the hand, that is surgery.
For the operation of the hand is prostrated in our region and in our time totally deprived, until the science of it has perished, and its practice is stopped; and there remain of it only a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which made the most errors and deviations to those mistakes and excesses until the intentions of it are closed and its force is elongated and the art.
And it seems to me that I will revive it with the ordering of this treatise in the second way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and so that it comes to the forms of the preparations of cauterization and of the other instruments of the work, as is necessary by addition of the declaration, and by preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the reason why no artisan is found skilled in this art in our time, is that the art of medicine is long and requires its practitioner to be exercised in the science of anatomy, which includes knowledge of the joining of the members and their forms, and the conjunction and separation of them; and has the understanding of the bones, nerves and ligaments, and their names, and their functions; and of the pulsating veins and the quiet ones, and the places of their emission.
And for this Hippocrates said that a small word is enough, especially in the work of the hand.
We have already spoken of that in the introduction to this book; for whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said regarding anatomy, it is not surprising that they fall into error, through which men die, as has been seen many times, because some are formed in this science and boast of possessing it, yet lack its practice and experimentation.
For I have seen a foolish and inexperienced doctor having made an incision on a scrophulous abscess in the neck of a woman, and having cut some arteries of the neck, through which a great amount of blood flowed, until the woman fell dead among his hands.
And I saw another doctor who ordered that he would swallow a stone of a man which was stuck in his throat, and the stone was large, and came to him and extracted that stone with a piece of the bladder, through which that man on the third day died.
And I have already called it foolish to extract that, and I saw that due to the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I suspected that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was paid by a duke of our land to perform surgery, and he applied a black plaster to a patient who had a fracture in their thigh; and the doctor, with his ignorance, extracted the fracture, put a poultice on the wound, with strong bandages and tight binding, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And return the dislocated according to the desires of the sick, and return the relaxed, and return the loose one for all joints and command that we untie the ligament; and it is necessary that thus between the thigh and the foot an abscess forms, and it comes to a dangerous loss.
And it is called relief for him, and prepared to dislocate the ligament, and acquired is tranquility and thus removed are his pains.
Greater corruption had already been confirmed in the member, for which it could not be restrained, and did not cease to spread the corruption in the member until the patient is in danger.
And I saw another doctor who made a cancerous abscess, and it was ulcerated in the following days, until the evil of it was magnified with the lord of it, his master.
This is because the bitter humor is pure melancholy, then it does not happen that it comes to him with all iron, but rather that it be in a member which suffers so that from it all is hosted.
And for this, sons, it is necessary that the operation with the hand be divided into two devotions: one is the operation in which health is associated, and the other is the work in which danger is in the greatest dispositions.
And you have already extracted this from every place of this book in which an operation is described where there is error and fear; for which it is necessary for you to guard against this and let go of that, so that the foolish do not accuse you of speaking and dishonesty.
And then take up your arms with solicitude and protection from God, and your patients with happiness and firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God to achieve health and praiseworthy success, and leave behind the terrible illnesses of difficult healing, and put away your arms from what makes you fearful, so that it does not diminish your faith and your name: for many are remaining for your glory, and may they be in the world and afterwards among your sanctities.
Indeed, I have already spoken to some wise men: Do not treat a bad illness poorly, so that bad doctors are not named".
And you have already devoted this book to three chapters.
Begin the division of the book, and first from the first part. The first chapter deals with the head and the feet, in the forms of instruments and in the preparations of cauteries, and what is necessary for the operation.
The division of the second section. The second chapter, on drying and perforation, and on ventoses, and on plasters, and on extraction of arrows and on similar things to them, all chapters and ordered according to the forms of instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and on treatment of twists and on similar things to them; chapter ordered from head to feet, and on the forms of instruments.
It is good to discern the quality of the juices of that cautery and of its instruments, and in which complication it is prohibited to apply cautery.
Therefore I say that the discourse on the quality of the juice of cautery and its instrument is a long and prolix discourse, subtle for science, and secretly hidden; and already many sages have spoken about it, and they are discordant, and for me it suffices to take a small part of their discourses, fearing prolivity.
And therefore I say that cautery is suitable for all universal complications, whether they are with material or without material, except for two complications, which are complications without material.
In the complex of the tail and dry matter, it will become disordered; because some said that a cauterized wound is helpful for this, and others said the opposite, that cauterizing is not convenient for an illness which is caused by heat and dryness, since the nature of fire is heat and dryness, and it is convenient that an illness of the tail and dry matter be treated with what is hot and dry to be healed.
And it is said by him who says the opposite, that cauterizing is made helpful in all dry and hot illnesses that occur in men's bodies, because when you compare men's bodies and their humidity to the complexity of fire, you find men's bodies are cold.
And I speak from the sermon of that one, who has already experimented on me several times to discover.
But I more openly declare that it is not necessary for that which has already been proven and practiced in the chapter of cauterizing through previous exercise, and having understood the diversity of the complexity of men and the disposition of their illnesses, and the causes of those, and the accidents of them, and the timing of those.
But in other complexities, it is not about your fear, and especially in cold and humid illnesses, because already all doctors agree on those, and are not disordered in the help with cauterizing in those.
It is known, sons, that the secret of curing by cautery with fire and the goodness of it, is that a cautery in medicine is burning, because the fire is simple, its action does not reach except to the member which is cauterized and it doesn't harm another member near it but only with a small injury.
More, the action of burning medicine reaches to that one in the members which is joined to it, and forces it to come into the sick member with difficult healing and forces it to be heard.
But the fire, by its subtle elevation and the goodness of its substance, does not make that which is superfluous; And it is known to us through experiment and through long duration of service in study of the art on the truth of the causes; and for this I am excused from the length of the sermon. And if it were not that my free will is bound by this secret, I would tell you about the fire, and the quality of its operation on bodies, and of its expulsion through which we expel sicknesses, in a philosophical demonstration, which would be acute in your understandings.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time in which it is convenient to do a cautery and they pause for the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because the harm from the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of that which the cautery attracts, and especially if the cautery is for pains or necessary pains, strong and frequent, which do not suffer delay so that it is feared that evil will come, which is greater than small harm entering through time.
And thus it is not seen in your steps, or, sons, that they esteem only the common people and foolish doctors, so it is that for that illness which is healed by cautery, all time is not required, and they pause to consider that consequence.
And the cause is not seen thus by them because they believe that cautery is only in place of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries the humors, which are the cause for which pains come.
More, I prefer cautery over medicine due to the will of its validity and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that the illness returns at some hour of time, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of their illness, and the virtue of it, and that which is prepared in the body from the aggregation of superfluities in it, and that which has come to it through food and habits similar to those causes; but that the illness in which cautery is administered is a subtle illness in a member with few superfluities and humors, thus as cautery of tooth for pain and similar to that, it is possible that in it the pain does not return, but rather it happens in a small place.
And most common speech is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is the speech of ignorant people, not because they understand it, but because they believe that there is no cure that can be achieved by medicine or any other cause except through cautery.
And the cause is to the contrary of that; and the intention that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is not unless when we administer the ways of cure in certain illnesses, and those medicines do not work, and then at the end of the cause, we administer cautery, and apply it to that. And therefore it is said that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish doctors understand.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the subtlety of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not burn, as it is not absolutely true, because it has been proven and found that it does not happen except in certain bodies besides the others, and cautery with it is good and better than with iron, as they said; but however when you make cautery with fire or gold, it is not declared to you, because it is ignited according to the quantity that you want for the roughness of the gold, and prepares to receive cold; and if you adjust it on the ember, the gold melts by the fire, and sometimes puts in the fire certain laminae so that the artisan can work with the occupation of it.
And for this, a cautery is made with iron, which we apply lightly and carefully to the rectitude of the operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter on the cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head between the feet, so that I alleviate the demanding one what he wants from it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization is opposed to humidity and cold on the service of the accidental one from which two causes are: it is a cause of swelling and multitude of flux, called rheumatism, of the head to the parts of the ears and of the hearing, and multitude of sleeping, and of toothache and of throat pain, and universally of all sickness that comes from cold, as well as paralysis, swelling, and apoplexy, and symptoms in those sicknesses.
The form of this cauterization is this: that first we command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine, for three or four nights, according to what the virtue of the sickness and the age of him and his custom require.
And then command him to shave his head with a razor, and then make him sit between your hands on a wooden bench and place your hands on his chest.
And then stop the flow of your palm's root near the nose's root between the heels of the shoes. More emperor, when the said inner part is perforated, mark that place with a probe, and apply the olive-tree cautery of which this is the form:
And then stop that on the place immediately with a probe, in a manner that descends, in which the inner hand is constricted little by little, and you turn it.
And then lift your hand slightly and examine the place, and if you see any part of the bone being uncovered to some extent, such as the quantity of a grain of barley, then lift your hand, and if it does not return to its former position, or if another part is cooled, until it is seen by the bone that which was said to you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve it on the place and apply it for three days.
And then stop on the cloth dipped in wax and apply it until the scar is destroyed by the fire. And then heal the place with Tetrapharmacum ointment until it is healthy.
And it is said that the more the wound is opened, the better and more youthful the arm will be, for which it is better.
They said that some of them should have the tendon cauterized within the bone, and a cautery should be held within it so that a part of the bone's vitality is taken away.
And then the part that is next to the bone should be scraped, and then it should be cured.
And they said that others should push the cautery from behind, so that it presses strongly into the bone, until the bone breaks, and this is the method of minor surgery: And they believe that from that place, vapors of the head are expelled.
And the open wound should be held for a long time, and then it should be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me, these two species of cautery have not been seen, except in some men according to the way of fear; and that, it seems to me, is better for health, because the head is revealed by solution of continuity of the urine as we have testified in other members, and especially when the head of the patient is of frail nature.
And the first species of cautery is safer and better, it seems to me; and from that practice and in that work, health is obtained.

Chapter 16.

Chapter 18.
Of cauterization of the fistula that is in the tear duct of the eye.
When you treat a fistula with the method that we have spoken of in the divisions of illnesses and do not confirm your treatment, then it is necessary that you cauterize it in this manner: order the patient to put their head back, and hold the head of the patient by some servant between the hands, in such a way that it is neither hidden nor agitated with the head back.

Chapter 39.
Of the extraction of blood associated with the knee.
When the knee is treated with medicine as we have said in the division of the cure with medicines and not with confectures, consider then on the knee of the patient to the sun, since you have compressed the tongue of it with an instrument that you have recommended.
Therefore, if you see the blood vessel, extract it with a small tool or with subtle gestures decently.
And if it is not possible for you to extract it, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the knee of the patient, and put in the cavity of the cannula an ignited iron, and do this as many times (until the blood vessel is dead and removed from the knee) and abstain the patient from water for the whole day.
And then take a full vessel of cold water, and put the mouth of it in that, and wash the mouth with that; and do not swallow any of this cause, but hold the water for an hour with your hand, because the blood vessel feels the water most when it is at rest.
More often if the patient is not previously prepared with what we have recommended, then subject the patient to a mixture of cypress or absinthe through the instrument that we have recommended in the suffumigation of the uvula.
Make this, then in four days.
And there is another manner of operation in the suffumigation of that, which you take a bowl in which are ignited coals and the bowl is covered with a cover in the middle of which is a hole, and the extremity of the instrument is composed in that hole; and apply it from below to the suffumigation; and put the patient's mouth on the extremity of the tube, and close their mouth so that the suffumigation is not expelled until you know that the suffumigation has reached the blood, because the blood then will discharge.
And if it does not descend, then repeat the suffumigation many times, and restrain the patient from drinking, and have them eat salty and bitter foods, and do not drink water, and it is necessary that with this treatment the suffumigation be expelled.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the blood of the throat is treated when it is visible; and it resembles a pair of pincers thus many times, except that it is in the alcove curved: Which is placed in the groin area, and the extremity of it resembles a beak of a stork, that is called gout, in which there is an accumulation of lime, for this reason, when we press any cause, it does not release.
Chapter 40.
In which there is the sum of the serum in collection of abscesses and in section of their discharge.
The abscesses are moved with special treatments, with various methods, according to the memory of them, of each one in this book.
And they are diverse in perforation and discharge of them through two methods, of which one is for the species of abscesses in themselves being treated; and for that which we press out of the humidity.
And the second method is proper for the places in which accidents of the body occur, because the abscess that happens in the head is different from the abscess that happens in the buttocks; and the abscess in the fleshy place is different from the abscess in the joint; and each of them is judged by operation.
And more of the abscesses are such that it is preferable that they not be perforated but rather have maturation of the blood in them or completion of it.
So other abscesses which are supposed to be pierced when they are ripe, and not matured according to their completion, just like abscesses that are applied to the joints, for an abscess that is near a joint, its being from it is prolonged until it reaches the purulent matter that is in the circuit of it, and for this reason the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, by which it is made cause of contraction of that member; or it is an abscess proper to a principal member, and if you delay the perforation of it until it is matured near the principal member; or it is proper to the anus, therefore perforate the unripe one; and it is not necessary to pierce the raw, undigested one, but only that which is proper to the anus, so that it does not press the rectum of it and is elongated to the parts divided from the anus, and a fistula is made, or that which is made in the term of it which is not sanated. It is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess, and also it is when it is matured.
And know that it is matured when there is a decrease in pain and a cessation of fever, and also a reduction in swelling and in pulse, and a sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs.
And where there is a cavity, you should know that the perforation creates a hole in the place of the abscess and of the pus coming from the treatment of the swelling.
And the perforation should be done through the length of the flesh or of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the hands or of the feet, and in the place of the veins, of the nerve cords, of the arteries; and, finally, in all hidden places where there is no reflection; because in those that are reflected, use perforation according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to delay the perforation until digestion is confirmed according to the humor, as we have said; because if you perforate then, it prolongs the body of the pus and of foul matter, and forces out the lips of the wound which become hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses should be perforated according to the width of the flesh or of the body as necessity dictates, or according to that which the affected member indicates.
And it is necessary to administer small perforations, and in large abscesses a large and wide perforation or several incisions according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And other times the apostemas are in those places where it is necessary that the abscess be opened and drained, when it is made thus as a poultice and made in term that has already suppurated, thus like that which falls into drops of pus and boils.
And of those that are cut with a section having three angles; and of those it is in which is incised thus as the figure of a leaf of mint, thus like the apostemas of the anginas.
And of them it is in those where a round section and a crescent-shaped section are administered, and similar to these.
More, that one which is not capable thus as are the superficial abscesses of the lion, where you should make a superficial perforation, or plane only.
And where the abscess is large and has collected much pus, that you should perforate it and not be concerned that you extract all the pus at that hour; having extracted from it a portion, and then apply a plaster to the abscess until the next day, and then extract a larger portion, and then make many evacuations according to the degree to which it is evacuated.
And especially if the patient is of frail virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old person in decline, because the animal spirit is greatly resolved with the egress of the pus, and hardly dies the patient, and you operate them.
Keep this chapter with great caution, and return your attention to the perforation in which you will make an incision, considering that you will clean the wounds and see if the wound of the abscess is small, or a flat cut, then you administer remedies of oil or anti-inflammatory ointment; and if the abscess is large, and the cracks of the perforation are many, then consider that you put a dressing on each wound so that they heal together.
And if in the abscess a part of the skin is separated or has formed a cavity, then consider that you fill it with a lot of soft cloth or yarn made from linen thread, as when you treat wounds or roots, its humidity; and apply this for three days; and then remove it and cure the area with what is necessary to heal the injuries.
But if there is an outflow of blood during the time of your operation, then you administer cold water and vinegar in which you soak a linen cloth, and place it over the area of the profusely bleeding wounds.
But if the bleeding persists, then consider that you administer treatment and cure with powders which have been recommended in many places of our book and division.
More so if it is in winter time, and the place of the abscess is a place of nervous movements, then it is good that you apply poultices made with wine and oil, and put them on those areas.
And if it is in summer, and the areas are fleshy, then it is good that you apply poultices soaked in water and oil or in wine and oil, and all that is applied should be cooled so that it is the third day, as we have said, and then it is good that you lance the abscess and cleanse it and administer to it the cure that is convenient for it.
And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the cure of abscesses in general, but according to the way of distinction I have already spoken of all abscesses in whatever manner is the way of the cure of them by chapters singularly.
Chapter twelve.
Of the section on abscesses that occur in the nape of the neck.
In the nape of the neck small abscesses form, and they are species of knots that contain tunics that are adherent to them; and the species of them are movable.
And some of them are cysts, and of those there are ones that contain humidity resembling slime. And of those which contain moisture similar to dust, and gather it; and of those which are muddy, rough.
And in the section of all, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, since you must not make the extraction of those cause irritation to the arteries.
And the operation in section of those is that you squeeze those with an instrument the shape of which goes near to them, which is called entromes, so that you know what they contain.
For if what it contains is moisture, then separate it in section according to the length by superficial section according to this form:
And begin in the section from line B to line G. Then when the moisture is evacuated, then you excise that which contains the moisture, and do not leave any of that cause of all, for if many times seen it returns, if it remains from that cause.
And then submerge the cot (knot or wound) in Egyptian gum, if it is present, and if not, in water and salt; and fill with that the wound and let it be until another day, for the corrosion of all that is made from that membrane.
And then apply on that wound the Egyptian gum secondly and thirdly if it is indicated for it, until you are confident that no longer is any cause of that membrane; then cure the wound with gum until it is healed.
And if there is an abscess with fatty nodes, then you insert the needle in this manner: I have made an incision in the shape of a cross, and placed forceps between the two lips of the incision and scraped out the entire affected area, and exerted my virtue in extracting the tunic which contains it.
More often if your bowels make counter-pressure, then do what you have previously recounted as primary.
And similarly do in the abscess of incision and cure according to what you have said; and an incision over a fatty abscess is considered lighter, because it is of little blood and little humidity.
And some times there are abscesses in the head of some men in whom there is absolutely no humidity; the cause of which is that I have incised over an abscess on the head of an old woman and found the abscess to be hard, rough, white, and dull, which could not be drained, and if I had struck it with a pustule, it would have burst.
But in other accidental abscesses on the head this is not the chapter, such as the abscesses that come to the heads of infants and from the roots of the ears, but the incision of all these should be superficial.
Stop the flow of those things from the lowest part of their body so that the body of the blood is alleviated to the lower parts.
And properly treat those with what is convenient for that cure.

It is of greater caution that the vein or nerve is not injured.

Chapter 43.
Of the section of the pill of the aposteme, accidentally taken by the apothecary.
The ancients said that this section was in the pill, and it was not seen by any man in our land that this had been done.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those.
More often in men there is a tendency to avoid the extraction of the stone, since it is not done gently, for which all the veins and main [blood vessels] of the patient are affected.
But in those who have abscesses or cuts in the mouth or throat or two ears, when the illness is not in the cane, it is advisable to use the section of the stone to flee the loss which is made by perforation.
Therefore it is advisable when we want to make an incision, that we cut the stone with three circles of the stone's circles, or four with a small section for the width in the one that is between two circles by quantity, so that the incision is in the cartilage-free area, not in the cartilage, and this place is convenient for incision, because it is deprived of flesh and the veins of blood from it are few.
And if the doctor is inexperienced, it is advisable that he extends the ligature of the throat with an onion, and then ties the ligature so that it comes to the canal, but avoids the blood vessels if any of them are visible for some reason.
Then incise the kidney as we have recommended; and it is indicated on the section of the canal by the weakness which is of that exit with what is of its disruption and by the abscessation of the mouth.
Elevate the wound that has been opened for some time.
Then when the hour is reached in which the perforation is feared, apply two lips of the gauze to the edge of the wound, and sew only that with the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that make the flesh grow so that it may be healed.
And Albucasis says that the sum of the sermon which we have recommended is not an exposition but rather to show that some of these apostems have already oppressed the throat of the patient, and the patient has come near death, and his life is in between, and some are about to obstruct the epiglottis so that the patient breathes on the place of the wound by some respiration, and be saved from death.
And therefore I command to leave the open wound until the evil of the disease is consumed; and its evil lasts for three days; and then I command to dress the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
And this that I have seen with my own eyes, is that a servant took a knife and put it in the throat and cut out a part of the vein of the lung, and I was called to its cure, and I touched the mucus as it is customary for the dead, and I uncovered the wound and I found the blood which had come out of the small wound.
Therefore, it was confessed that a vein or ligament had not been injured, and the wound was from the plague, and they cured it before the focus became infected.
And do not hasten to serve if it does not arrive at the desired time, and then return after some days to the improvement of their conditions.
And now I say that in the removal of the splinter there is no fear.
Chapter 44.
Of the incision regarding the aposthema which occurs in the throat before, and it is called throat hernia.
This apostema called throat hernia is a large aposthema according to the body's coloring, and it is common in women.

And the natural one is not worthy of a cure.
And the accidental one is said in two ways, of which one is similar to fat knots, and the other way is similar to an aposthema which is made by knotting of an artery, and in that one there is fear. Chapter twelve.
Of the section of the species of knots.
Of the knots, many species and I have already said all the species of them in the division.
And I recommend that you recount thus the difference between a knot and an abscess with certain doubtlessness.
Therefore I say that with an abscess there is heat and fever and violent pains until the ebullition of the surplus is sedated; and it is a completed putrefaction which then ceases the fever, the pain and the heat.
But with a knot there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that pus which is in its own sac.
And it is according to the color of the body, and its beginning is like a cyst and is made thus as a vacuity, whether major or minor, and they are according to two species, which are either fat or contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, as I have said in the division.
Therefore I say, when you come to the cure of a knot, that you expel that and inquire into its beginning with an instrument which is called an intrument, as will be seen in the chapter which is next.
And it is the method of inquiry into abscesses and all knots, and it is that you take this instrument and insert it into the humid place which you find in the abscess, and you will turn the threads of the needle little by little until you know that the instrument has penetrated the kernel.
And then put your hand according to the measure of the greatness of the abscess, and extract the entrails and consider what is coming out from the remains of it.
And if the flowing humidity is forgotten, of whatever color it may be, then you dry it with a superficial drying according to what has been said about other abscesses.
And if from the remains of the entrails there is no humidity, then you should know that it is fat.
And dry on it with drying having the shape of a cross according to this shape: thus as you have been taught, and suspend that which is excessive, and scratch the crust from all parts with ease, and keep the skin or sack, if you can, over that and extract that blood from the knot.
But if it is broken during the operation, it is not possible to extract that blood, and many times it happens that this occurs, and then you extract it by pieces until none of it remains.
For if some of it remains for any reason, a little or too much, the knot returns according to the worse.
And if you see that some small part of it remains, then complete the wound with some sharp corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, and apply a cauterized dressing on the area where the abscess was, and cure that with another treatment until it is healed.
And if it is a large knot, then kiss the patient's lips and cure that which grows in the flesh.
If the pulse is rapid in the patient, or slow, then touch and fill the place of the third finger with a poultice made from vitriol and apply it for two or three days until the plague disappears and the swelling of the blood subsides; and then return to cut away that which is rotten from the knot.

Chapter 47.
On the treatment of men's breasts which are similar to women's.
Certain men have swollen breasts which are caused by excessive sleep and poor diet, and as a result their breasts become swollen and similar to women's, and it is considered shameful.
And to the one who has this condition, it is necessary to make an incision on the breast in the lunar section according to this form, from line B to line G, and then remove all the excess flesh, and fill the wound with incarnate medicine, and sew the two lips of the wound together with stitches, and heal the one inside until they are cured.
But if the breast declines to the sides and is softened by its size, similar to that of women, then it should be divided into two parts, with two sections resembling a lunar figure, each one contained in the other up to the end of each, so that the larger section contains the smaller one according to this form, from line B to line G. And then remove the flesh that is between the two lips of the wound, and remove the excess fat, and administer what we have said about the stitches and powders, whatever is necessary for the cure until it is healed.
And if you do not complete the incision of what must be cut due to the anxiety of the patient, and because of an outflow of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with a submersed plaster in a corrosive ointment and lay on that which corrodes the rot of the fracture, and properly cure that which is affected by the disease.

Chapter 49.
On the section of abscesses that occur by acridity or by vein.
When the artery is broken, and the vein is consolidated which is above it, then putrid abscesses are suspected, and the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscesses are from the artery or from the vein: for when an abscess is from the artery it is long and accumulated in the thorax of the body; and when you press the abscess with your fingers, you feel a stridor in the vein.
And that which is from the vein is round at the surface of the body.
And a section about this abscess is an error, especially in that which is near the shoulders, and in the armpits, and in the neck, and in many places of the body; and it is very bad, therefore it is necessary that its treatment be avoided with iron, and that which is in the extremities, or at the head, it is necessary that it be avoided.
More about that which is from the flow due to inflammation of the arterial orifice, incision in the vein section in the long; and then make an incision with knives and then reveal the artery, and removal of the tunics until it be discovered.
And then put the needle on that thread and make it penetrate between the other sides, and tighten the ligature with double fidelity in two places,  which causes you to extract the excess humors from the temples.
And then touch the place which is between two ligaments with spatula so that the blood comes out from it, and let the abscess be dissolved.
And then administer the cure in which pus is generated until the ligaments fall; and treat that with a suitable ointment for that, so that it will be healed.
And if it is an abscess due to a cut vein, then take care that you hold with your hand the thing that is nearest to the abscess on the side of the body, and put the needle in the place where you have held your hand, and make it penetrate; and let it be in the double thread by which you extract from one side, and tie the abscess with a good ligature as I have told you in the ligature of the uva, on two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then put the thread in the needle before all the abscess goes out of the first incision, and tighten the threads in four places.
Then dry the abscess in the middle place of the entry that when it comes out what is in it, afterwards you cut the excess of the quiver, and let out what is bound to it.
And apply a poultice on it that has been submerged in wine and oil, and administer the cure that is made with warm compresses and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter one of the abscess which occurs due to twisting of nerves.
Thus as the abscess occurs in the artery and in the vein, similarly the abscess occurs in the nerves when it occurs due to their percussion or when it occurs from excessive effort, and from similarities.
And it is made worse by it in the places of the joints or of the ankle, or in any place where the articulations are flexed.
And it is a severe abscess, and it resembles the color of the rest of the body, and it is in the worst of its conditions six of them and when it is constrained with inflammation, it seems to the patient similar to stupidity.
And it is not an abscess that gathers in the front of the body, and for this reason the quiver is applied, and it is increased on one side and does not go to the sides either from the front or from the back.
Therefore, it is not suitable for those who have joint pain to be treated with iron, because the treatment would cause a strong contraction.
Pain in the head or forehead is treated with a plaster. If it is a mild abscess, then apply warmth and separate that which is putrid from the root.
And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and excavate that, and apply an ointment to that; and adjust the wound with a suture, and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter 51.
On the section of abscesses that occur in the spleen which occur near the belly.
We find in some men fatty growths in the bellies of those and in other parts of the body of those that have spleens which are called fungal due to similarity with fungi, of which the root is subtle and the head is thick; and already the lips of those are turned, and it is of those that are small, and it is of those that are very magnified.
And I have already seen one, and in the belly of it there were two spleens which were more similar to fungal growths, and there was no difference between those whites, of minimal root.
And already the lips of those were turned inward and were split, and moisture flowed from them all the time.
Then I inserted a probe into them and inserted one in the foot with eighteen threads, and another with six threads.
And the operation on the incision of them is that you consider then if the patient is humid, and the color of the tissue is white, humid, with subtle roots; then you insert a spatula in the wound, and have cauteries in the focus, for four to six times the section of it will expel its humor; and if the humor comes out, cauterize that.
And if the patient is pale and fearful, guard yourself from incision with iron; but then take a piece of fresh lead, and apply it to that tissue, the handling of which is what we have said; and leave it for two days.
And then adjust in the constriction of the thread of lead; thus, do not cease to apply the large lead plaster on the tissue, until it is absorbed and falls off by itself with its own effort.

Chapter 76.
On the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with the method we have mentioned in the division of medicine and it is not an emergency, and you are not forced to use operation, then consider if the woman is of good virtue and not at risk for accidents by which there would be danger to her.
Then it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back on a seat or chair, with her head inclined downwards and her thighs elevated.
And the operator should hold the woman's two parts or tie her to the seat so that her body does not move during the extraction of the fetus.
And immediately anoint the mouth of the matrix (womb) with oils, mucus, and extracts of wormwood, fenugreek, and sesame.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucus, and then inserts her hand with ease into the womb, and then feels for the place where the fetus is stuck.
And place conveniently in that: then consider if the foot is prepared that you will put on the head, and then you fix the nails in the heels of it, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or give the beard, or in the throat of it, or in the proper places of the ribs, or give the hips.
More if the putting is on the feet of it, then in the knee, or in the middle of the ribs.
And take that you hold the nail with your right hand, and pause the curvature of it in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and introduce the hand with ease and put the nail in some of those places that we have said, until it reaches the hollow cause.
And then pause and put on the application of it another nail, or the third if it is necessary, so that it be equally attracted, and not extended according to its straightness just as much.
Until the hand is moved to the entire affected part, so that the weight of it be alleviated thus as it is done in two ways for the eradication of it.
And take in that which is between them that the extension be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then take that the midwife anoints some of her fingers with oil and introduces them skillfully and stirs with those fingers in that place that is retained.
Therefore, if the part of the foot is forgotten, then the ankles should be anointed with a remedy to be put in that place; and do so until the entire foot is treated.
But if the hand is stuck to the other, and it's not possible to reduce it by constriction, then it's necessary that a bandage be wrapped around it; and carefully extract it until it's all treated, and incise it either in the joint of the hand or in the elbow.
And do the same on the other hand and on the two feet.
But if the head of the foot is large, or adheres to the constriction in the extremity, or is at the head of the water adjusted, then it's necessary that an intermediate spatula be inserted between the toes and the head be opened and the water extracted, or that it be scraped with an instrument called alundat, the shape of which will be described along with the shapes of the other instruments in the chapter that is appropriate to this.
And do the same if the foot has a naturally large head: then it's necessary that it be incised with a chisel, or that it be scraped with an alundat as we have said; and carefully extract the bones with the forceps.
And if the head is elevated and constricted by the armpit, then it should be cut open so that the humidity which is in the chest can be expelled.
More or less, if it's not complicated, nor does it obstruct breathing, then you should raise the head as much as is possible for you.
And if the abdomen is swollen with abscesses or it is dropsical, then it is necessary that you perforate that area through which the humidity that is in it can flow.
More or less, if the fetus is positioned above the two feet, then its attraction is to the left and its direction to the mouth of the womb is to the left.
More or less, if it is constricted by the abdomen and chest, then it is necessary that you extract that which is wrapped in a cloth, which you have placed over your hand, and that you cut open the abdomen and chest so that what is in them can flow out.
More or less, if the other members are stopped and the head is turned, then the midwife inserts her left hand; more or less, if the mouth of the womb is open, then she inserts her hand into the middle of the womb, and pulls towards herself the head, and draws that which is with the fingers into the mouth of the womb, and inserts in it one or two inches, and draws it towards herself.
And if the mouth of the matrix is constricted by a posthumous cauterization which adheres to the urine, then it is good that there not be trouble upon it; moreover it is good to administer an infusion of humid and fatty causes. Then administer plasters; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fever is on the sixth day, then if possible, it should be pricked: and there should be administered what we have said in the case of the living liver.
And if that is not possible, then let it be cut into slices, and extracted.
And it is good that no cause of the interior be left in the secondine ( likely referring to a part of the body or an organ).
And when you have completed all your operation, then administer what we have said about the cure in the aposthems (or abscesses) that adhere to the matrix.
And if there is an issue of bloody flux, then dip in astringent waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in whose belly was a dead fetus, and then upon that womb another conceived and pregnant one, and the dead fetus is the other. It happens to him that for a long time an abscess forms in his sick intestine; and it becomes inflamed inside where the focus is opened, and begins to take arms.
And he was called to his cure, and treated for a long time, and the wound is not consolidated.
Then he applied to him from several causes a plaster of strong attraction, and extracted from him a bone, and then passed through his intestines, and extracted another bone; and it was greatly marveled, since in the belly there is not a bone.
And then he thought that they were bones of a dead fetus.
Then he probed the wound, and extracted from it many bones, a woman existing in her intestines with thousands of dispositions, and already lived in such a manner for a long time, correcting from him a little arm.
And he did not find it strange, but rather that in this there is science and help to him who the doctor artificially makes by hand for the purpose of cure.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Shape of a vertebra in which the matrix is opened:
This is the shape of a holder in which the liberties are wrapped, to which wrapping two vertebrae are joined at both extremities of two thighs. May the emperor grant this virtue with what is subtly drawn from the strictor, and made either of ebony or of beechwood.
And the width of each staff is two fingers and the thickness of each one is a finger, and the length of each one is a palm and a half; and in the middle place of two staffs there are two adjustments of the same wood, which are already fixed, of which the length is a little more than half a palm, and the width of each one is two fingers, or a little more.
And these two additions will be inserted into the mouth of the mother so that it is open to those when you administer the two prescribed virtues.
Make another similar form to that one, but more subtle and lighter:
Let it be made of ebony or beechwood staffs according to the similarity of the forces. May the emperor have at the extremity of it two additions thus many times, and the length of these additions is about a palm, and the width of each one is two fingers.
And when you want to open the mother with these, then you will make the woman raise her legs, hanging them from the bed, opening that which is between her thighs. And then take your hand with the instrument in such a way that you make an incision according to the quantity that you want of the thickness of the mouth of the matrix, until the meter makes what you want.
The form of vertigo which the ancients called:
Form of inflammation by which the foot is swollen:
Form of friendship by which the big head is congested
And it is assembled with forceps to which the teeth are in the extremity, like scissors, and some times it is made long like forceps according to this form, like scissors, to which the teeth are like teeth of rescue on which it has been incised and congested. Form of small friendship:
Form of a wound having a spine:
Form of a wound having two spines:
Form of a spatula having two extremities, on which the head is cut off:
Form of two broad spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when they are multiplied, the species of that one are prepared by the artisans, as much as it is easier for their operation and more useful to men because of their quantity.
And do not think that those instruments are yours to wield, for the necessity of them is not an excuse.
Of the extraction of the secondine (or possibly "the afterbirth").
When the afterbirth is retained, you must command the patient to retain it, and make her throw up with condiments, and hold your hand over her mouth and nostrils, and if by doing so it does not come out, well.
And if not, then take a woolen cloth and perforate in the cover a hole and put on that opening of the mouth of the matrix, thus as calamint and rue and anise and chamomile and aristolian and cassia wood and holy tree. Soak all these herbs or some of them in water in the cloth, and place that over the womb.
And then put a cane tube in the mouth of the matrix, and hold it there until the vapor comes to the cavity of the matrix.
And make her throw up as we have said, and the afterbirth will be expelled with speed.
But if this cure is not effective, then you command the midwife to immerse her left hand in oil of juniper or in extract of wormwood, and then insert it into the womb and search for the afterbirth, and when she has found it, then take it out piece by piece. But if it is stuck in the matrix's perineum, then insert the hand as we have recommended, and when she has found the afterbirth, extract it little by little according to the rule so that the matrix does not fall into vehement pain. Above all, it is desirable that the right and left costs be permeated with ease.
And if the mouth of the matrix is constricted, we have already recommended the cure with purging and medication of the bile with herbs.
But if it is not forgotten for all the causes that we have recommended, then beware that you do not perform on that in iteration of abstraction, but rather it is desirable that what is excreted from it to the mouth of the matrix lies at the thigh of the woman, and then anoint that with gum and tetrapharmacon; because that will make her purge for several days and it will be dissolved and it will be forgotten.
But when it is purged, it rises from it to the head and to the stomach, and that torments the patient; and then it is desirable that sub-fumigations and conveniences be administered to it.
But some of the Ancients already used a sub-fumigation of dried nasal roots and of dried fig leaves.
Form of an instrument with which the woman is fumigated for the retention of menses and of the afterbirth:
It must be made from a vein or artery.
And let the thin extremity be placed in the pot and the wider extremity over the fire, and the sub-fumigation be placed on the arms of the fire.
And hold that in until the sub-fumigation is consumed and another one is put in its place.
On the treatment of the navel of an unperforated infant.
Many infants are born and their navels are not perforated, which have a thin and closed cicatrix. Then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce with a needle that navel, and if not, she should pierce it with a sharp spatula, and be careful not to touch the liver.
And immediately apply on that place a flannel cloth soaked in wine and oil; and treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
But if you fear that it is closed, then insert a small tube into the navel for many days, and block it when the infant needs to cry.
And if there is closure of the navel due to consolidation of a wound or an abscess; then it is necessary that this consolidation be cut, and immediately treated with what we have said about the treatment and the plaster.
About the cure of fistulas that occur in the eyes.
The fistulas that appear in the lower part of the eye are a sign of a bad and gross tumor, which appears near the anus or in the space of one side.
And it is a fistula or many tumors.
And when that tumor is old and rotten from the moist whitish or subtle decay, and some of these fistulas are seen to be penetrating.
And those penetrating ones are known by what is exiting from them through discharge and flatulence; and some times the patient uses the discharge, and it is forced out of them with worms.
And some of these fistulas are seen to be penetrating in the space, entering into the bladder, and entering into the flesh of the penis; and some of these penetrations enter into the joint of the thigh and into the nut of the scrotum.
And that in which a penetrating fistula is recognized entering into the anus and non-penetrating, is that you put your finger inside the anus, and you insert a thin thread of wool or iron into the fistula when it is not suppurating.
But if there is suppuration in it, then insert into it a thin thread of lead or horsehair that you feel with your finger.
And if you do not feel the whole of it nor any process of the gut causing any expulsion or worm or gas, thus as we have said, then know that it is non-penetrating, and then hasten to the cure.
When the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the flesh of the penis, then the meaning of it is emission of urine from that and prohibition of it to such an extent that the place be consolidated with medicine.
More so if it is penetrating into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and increases pain in the circuit, then the sign of it is that the tendon is perforated inside here if there isn't fracture inside the bone, and increase of pain in the circuit of the affected part; and that of it is purulent discharge; and that it doesn't respond to medication, nor is consolidated with plaster.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no cure for everything, and the cure of those is labor and vainness of the foolish doctors regarding which they boast.
But in that which is not penetrating and not ancient, health with iron is hoped for, according to what you have recommended, and that which has already been tried and proven.
And it is that the patient goes between your hands over the back of theirs and raises their legs inside them, the thighs bent to their belly, and then insert a probe of lead, or of iron if there is fracture in the fistula, so that you can feel the place where the tendon is perforated.
And if that sense of the patient turns around the neck, then it is necessary that you insert your finger inside the neck.
And if you feel with your finger the tendon already exposed and uncovered to penetrate, or what you feel between the tendon and that sinew or flesh, then be certain that this is the penetrating one; and do not work on that, because it is not in that place the healing, as we have said.
More often doctors say that there are healthy parts in some men's thighs.
And for the treatment by which healing is hoped for, you should make a subtle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as previously described, and insert that ignited thing into the fistula until it reaches around the neck; and then turn it two or three times until you know that all those adjusted flesh, formed into fistulas, are adhered, resembling a feather of a bird.
And then treat that wound with bandages wrapped in gauze until all the adjusted flesh is united, and then treat it with medicines that engender and consolidate the flesh, and if it heals, well; and if not, then it is not healed in a suitable time for another treatment.
And if the probe enters, and does not penetrate into the intestine of the said thing which is in the anus, and between that and the probe which is a thin piece of flesh or of tissue, and sometimes the fistula in what is the surface of the codena, then cut the codena from the beginning of the fistula, and you will have cut with the probe, and it will be in the fistula until the section reaches the place where the extremity of the probe appears, and through the probe it is liberated and extracted.
Then carefully clean those fistulated flesh wounds which are assembled to the channel of the needle and do not break any of those channels for fear that it may cause complications.
More often if there is a flow of blood or pus that comes between you and your operation when you dissect those flesh wounds, then the milk that will be is from the instrument to cauterize with fire or with acute medicine, for cauterizing with fire adjusts good habits: it is adjustment of those adjusted flesh, and removal of the bloody excretion of humidity.
And then heal that wound which is covered in bandages or in dressings within the place where the arm is, and then heal the wound with gum or with hard flesh that generates and consolidates.
And thus medications are applied in which there is stipulation and purging; when the hour is restored it is already healed and you do not fear relapse.
More often if the fistula has passed into the anus and is extended from the surface of the body, then insert the finger into the anus and ask about that.
And then if you feel the tension and between you and it is a veil of skin or of flesh, and it is ready for penetration, then it is not an operation on it but rather a way of trust and of hope.
This cause is to administer in it one of three manners: either that you cauterize it thus as we have said; or that you purge it within until you achieve its cavity so that it is possible for you to insert the instruments and the prepared cure; and do not proceed with more purging than necessary so that you do not irritate the containing lacert, and that you act above the patient's will; and then treat it with what we have said before, since it will be strong; or that you extend this veil and remove the pus that you purge within near the anus, thus as we have said, either with the finger or with another sharp instrument, and then cleanse those fistulized flesh which are in the purged area where you can perforate; and then strive to make the restoration of the entire wound with purging, and if the underlying pus is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open in the part of the anus, it will be easier for the patient. And certain fistulas are finished in this manner: it is when you insert the tent into the fistula, and it is in the flesh of the buttocks around the surface of the body with the cod and in the margin of the buttocks, then take the tent of the perforated extremity, which is like a needle for preparing the orifices according to this form:
and insert it into that vein wrapped with five veins or around those; and then insert the tent into the vein in the fistula until it achieves the cavity of it.
More if it is penetrating the margin of the buttocks deeply, then you extract the vein from that hole so that you insert your finger in the buttocks; and extract the extremity of the vein and adjust the two extremities together, and tighten each one, and leave it for a day or for two, and when you press the vein into the flesh, tighten both until those fleshes are pressed which are between the two extremities of the vein and which fall.
And then cure the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
More if the orifice of the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate, in whatever manner you are prepared, but let it be moved by the groin, for it is not for you to do this so that the lacert does not press; and then do this until it is healed.
The form of the spatula is spiked at the end where the fistula is divided: its curvature is very sharp and the other part is not sharp, so that it does not insert unnecessarily, thus as needed.
Of suture of hemorrhoids in which runs blood in the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are according to two methods, either between the buttocks or what is of carbuncles, or if those are with fat of rushes. And of those are small and large, and the blood runs from those tumors and it is one, and very painful, and outside the anus, and in the extremities of it.
Worse are those that are outside the anus according to the measure of little humidity, from which runs yellow water or a little blood with continuous flow, and according to the color of the body.
And the cure of that which is next to the anus is that you command the patient to sit and to press inside so that the anus opens and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take and suspend with force or you hold those with your fingernail, and then you cut those according to their roots.
If the ulcers are not held in those places by the humidity and softening of them, then take those with a coarse cloth or with a cotton swab or with a flannel of wool, and extract those with the fingers, and return to put on top of them some powders, dusting over them some cauterizing powders near the incision, so that they are held in place of a cautery; or cauterize those as it was explained in the chapter about cauterization. And then heal those with another cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey to evacuation, then anoint the patient with a cluster in which there is a mild purging, and let it be washed with that water which is in the basin and which will make the anus evacuate more easily when the patient strains.
If the hemorrhoids are very painful in the anus, then the cause of them is the easiest to cure, and it is that you take those with your fingernail, or that you take those with a needle, and insert those, and then heal those with the water that we have mentioned until they are healed.
And for the one that has an incision, it is necessary to administer a suture of them in this manner: take thread and pass it through the needle and then extract the hemorrhoids from the divisions above, and make that penetrate with the needle into the root of the other part, and wrap the two extractions of the thread around the division behind the needle, and longitudinally; and tighten the hemorrhoid with strong structure, and then knot the thread and extract the needle.
Make a cut in that area, and let out one of those, but not the marrow, so that the excess blood from that vein may flow.
Then place a poultice made from rose oil or wax on the buttocks, and put that on the anus, and command the patient to rest. And let it enter into that wound; and when it is digested, treat those with an ointment or with another cure so that they may be healed.
And since they are old and of no value in that medicine, it is fitting that you treat those with the application of spit or with your nail into which moisture is made, and let the dirty pus be expelled from them, which prevents them from consolidating; and then treat those so that they may be consolidated.
Then apply those with a violent purging that the first one enters much blood and they are scraped off; and then treat those so that they may be healed.
It is known that the ulcers of the nostrils are clear, and not otherwise, unless noted by a redness according to the color of the body resembling a head of nails, and it is made in all the body and especially in the parts below the feet and the toes, and it comes from those joint pains.
And then it is necessary that what has grown in the circuit of the claw be taken hold of with the tongs or with an iron clamp, and be eradicated from its root; and then treat that.
And if you want, cauterize the second one that is mentioned in the following chapter.
More precisely, a wart is a small, rough, rounded, and fistulated protrusion on the surface of the body, and similar growths appear on the hands of children.
And the treatment for it is to stretch or cut that out, or to tighten that with a thread or a probe that fits inside. And if you want, cauterize that, as we have said, with fire or with sharp medicine.
More precisely, ringworm is a small, fuzzy, or fistulated thick growth on the surface of the body, especially on the thigh, and when it touches that it seems to be inflamed in the likeness of an ulceration of ringworm, and it is found around the body.
And the treatment for it is to take a needle of cotton thread or of wool thread, and let it be strong, and pass it over the ringworm until it contains the circle of the thread with the parts that surround it; and then insert your hand with the needle into the area surrounding the ringworm, and push that into the thigh of the flesh, and eradicate the ringworm from its root.
And if you want, make this with a cane of brass or iron according to this form:
Let the part of the cane that penetrates have subtlety, be blunt (that is not perforated), wrapped in such a way that on the said thing the absorption of it is alleviated and the revolution of that.
And if you want, cauterize the ant hill according to what is stated in the cauterization of the sore in the chapter on cauterization.
Of the form of the instruments that are administered to give relief.
Some poultices are made of silver or gold or melted or beaten brass; and some poultices are made from those small and large instruments according to those for which they are administered, because that which is administered in the cure of small children should be small; and for those whose buttocks are cold or painful, their poultices should be small.
The form of large and few poultices:
The head of the cane where the bag is tied should be wide in this manner; and let the distinction be where the bag is tied, thus many times.
And the extremity of the part that is inserted in the buttocks, which is penetrating, should be blunt (that is not pointed), smooth to subtlety; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole, and let the width of the hole be according to the thickness of the rods and a little thicker.
And let the bag be in which are placed the medicines of bladder of beast or of skin of sheep, and its size be a palm.
And let it be perforated by many holes thus as it is rolled up; and if the space which is between the holes is the thickness of the said.
And then insert into those holes a strong and crude filament which should be of twelve filaments, or wrap around those; and adjust to it the bag; and when the bag is placed on it, let it be tight at the head of the patient between two distinguishing strengths with forced constriction, and then constrict each hole: The quality of constricting for that is that you fill the bag with medicine, which should be warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the patient; and beware that it not be too hot nor too cold.
And then the patient should be raised on their back, and lift their legs up and place under them a cushion on which are already the men or a plank; and anoint the extremity of the cautery with oil or with white of egg or with mucus of fenugreek or of similar things; and then insert that into the anus with facility, and then the minister takes the bag and expresses it with two fingers and strongly with violence until everything that is in the gut is evacuated from the bowel; and then remove the gut and the patient lifts their legs to the wall.
And if the medicine forces out the excess, hold it in as much as possible; and if you sleep on it for an entire night, it is more beneficial in treatment.
More so if you treat it in diseases of abdominal discharge and its evacuation, then you will apply the cautery until it is healed.
And if in the anus there are painful hemorrhoids or abscesses, then let the treatment be subtle and gentle, of the treatments with which the children are treated.
On the treatment of wounds.
I have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds what is suitable for the free, and I say thus the treatment of those with medicine according to the complement.
Therefore, I say that wounds are diversified according to what they are made of and according to the place where the wound occurs.
And the causes by which many wounds are made are like this: a blow with a stone, or a cut with a sword, or with a knife, or a hit with a lance, or with a fist, or with an arrow, or similar to those of many causes.
More wounds that are in the places of the body are like this: a wound on the head, or the neck, or the chest, or the abdomen, or the liver, and similar to those of the limbs.
And thus we recommend the treatment of certain wounds for which we pause this reasoning and rule over other wounds.
And we will begin with the simple head wounds, for the discussion of the composite ones will come to the commentary of the third chapter.
Thus I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is due to a blow from a stone or something similar, and the skin has only been scratched and it is a large wound and you fear the onset of an apostemic infection, then you should be cautious and perform a cephalic bloodletting at once, and do not delay; and extract from that vein according to the quantity of the virtue needed by the patient, unless there is some prohibitive cause for bloodletting, especially if the blood that exits from the wound is scarce.
And let the bloodletting be on the opposite side of the wounded part; and protect the patient from replenishment and from wine and from coarse foods.
But if some cause prohibits minor bloodletting, then let it be reduced from the diet and not approached with meat nor wine.
And apply to the wound, if an apostemic infection occurs, cotton soaked in rose oil or in wine in which is added a styptic.
More surely if it is secure to apply a hot poultice, then pause on the wound, if it is recent with blood and the air has not altered that powder which you will recommend to apply in a small amount.
And if the air has already changed it, then pause on other soothing ointments until it is healed.
More if the wound is large or is by incision of tissue and of similar things, and the lips of it are not adjusted by threads, then adjust them with a suture as you will recommend from the suture of others.
More if the wound has already exposed the bone and flesh, and it is not retained by them but only a small suspensor, then incise that and treat the wound with medicines and restore the flesh properly in place of decayed tissue, and command the patient to abstain from foods in which there is coarseness: cabbage and beans and similar things to them, until it is healed.
And if you find in the decayed tissue putridness and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all that rotten part and throw it away, and treat the area.
More if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which a flow of blood can come, and it is not stopped by medicines, then inquire about the artery, and if you find it uncut, then cut it with a spatula, or tie it; and if necessity provokes that what we have said does not suffice, then cauterize until the blood is stopped.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is an ulceration; thus you should powder over those wounds a powdered substance, which consolidates and heals them before the air touches them.
And the method of the powder is this: take oil of iris one part, dragon's blood two parts, and unslaked lime three parts; grind everything together and crush it, and fill the wound with it, and constrain it with a good bandage so that it stays on the affected area, and coagulate it with the blood.
Then tightly bind the dressing with pulvils and leave it, and do not remove it while it is like this so that it does not become infected, for the medicine is not eradicated from it until it is healed.
And sometimes this sole treatment is enough, when you have at hand iris and dragon's blood.
And this medical operation is performed on large wounds when it is convenient to place it on them and they are constrained, and also on recent wounds with their own blood, which the air has not yet altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially in summer, then it is not suitable for the application of this powder, but rather cure them with what we have said, so that you apply on them some digestive ointments, or apply on them powders made from wheat flour mixed with water and honey until they form a paste; and then cure them with another treatment until they are healed.
Mainly if the fracture occurs in the bone and is small, then you extract it with gestures.
And I will describe the treatment of head fractures in that which is poisonous.
Of the sores of the neck.
Mainly if the sore occurs on the neck, then it is not different in medication, and between the sore of the head when it is simple.
Mainly if the nerve of the neck is cut or an artery, then if it is a nerve, it is not in the remedy but rather the treatment should be avoided with that which causes vehement constriction, thus as to say and to warn that it is poison and similar to their destruction because it harms the nerves and contradicts them. And do not put anything on the sore that causes total freezing, because the substance of the nerves is fragile and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest of all members.
And if it is treated with light medicines, such as being washed with warm water, some ointment rubbed in oil or not-rubbed, and turpentine when it is washed with warm water and the other dressings made according to this manner, and anointed with humid.
If the wound is large, then administer a suture, or sew up the lips of it, and immediately cure that with powders so that it may be healed.
If the wound has depth or reaches to the lowest part of the body, then perforate it in the place most depressed.
If an artery has already been cut in the wound and a flow of blood is obtained, then stop it or ligate it, or tie it, or cauterize it if necessity requires it.
If the tendons of the shoulder or all have been cut, and the veins of the neck are saved, then you adjust the lips of the wound with suture on the edge of the shoulder and do not touch that; afterwards put it back in its natural shape, and immediately strengthen it with a decent dressing, and leave it for several days; and immediately cure it with an ointment in which there is stimulation and excitation so that it may be healed.
If the wound has already formed a scab on the bone, then pierce it, and if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all that you can; and what you cannot remove, leave it until the wound becomes purulent, and it will be separated and the pressure of it will be alleviated.
And if the wound is recent, then powder on that powder which is recommended to you. More so if in the wound there is made a fistula, then cure it with that which memory will bring back to the seventh chapter.

And take care to restore it on the first day of the fracture, if possible; and if not, then apply the vinegar or the decoction of the healing plant to the rest of the aposteme.
And then insert into the end of the nose a thread of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part, or two threads, if the fracture is in two parts, and let it be in the thread enough quantity to fill the hole of the nose.
And some of the ancient restorers said that the threads should be soaked in borax, and should be applied throughout the day, but it is not seen by me; however, it is necessary that the thread be wrapped in a poultice of honey combined with powdered mallow; and then leave the thread until the bone is fixed and the cartilage is hardened.
And sometimes insert into the nostrils certain warm compresses, in place of heat, a poultice made from a mixture of wool and lion's skin; and make sure that you have already applied the fracture of the nose strongly and that the patient is not prohibited from breathing.
And this cause is not necessary for you; and if you want to, do it, and if you want to, apply warmth.
And if a severe abscess or boil occurs, plaster the nose with wax or with a mixture of melted wax and rose oil, or with a diaculum.
But if a severe abscess or boil does not occur, then take care to plaster the affected area with flour of euphorbia and powder of crushed almonds mixed with white album of egg; and place a poultice on the stoppage, and do not bind the nose for any reason.
But if the bones of the nose are broken with a small fracture or are comminuted, then take care to split apart those, and extract those with instruments that are suitable for those; and place a bandage on the fissure, and cure it with water that nourishes and consolidates, and plaster it with what is conveniently applied.
And if an ulcer occurs inside the nose, then take care to cure it with warmth and administer suppositories of lead until it is completely healed.
Chapter Four.
On the restoration of the jaw when it is fractured.
When the jaw is broken and the fracture of it is not a serious wound, consider then if the fracture is only displaced and not broken in two and is curved to the separated parts within, then its union is easier.
And do this, if the fracture is on the right side, you will insert your left index finger into the patient's mouth; and similarly if the fracture is on the left jaw, then insert the right index finger of the right hand; and press with that the curvature of the fracture within to facilitate the displaced parts coming together, with your other hand on the outside of the bone; and gently move them so that they come together.
And if the fracture of the jaw is already separated into two parts, then it is necessary that you apply extension to both parts according to the correct method until it is possible to bring them together.
And if it happens with the displacement of teeth to disruption, then hold those with which you expect to remain firm with a thread of gold or silver or silk; and place a bandage over the fractured jaw, and place a bandage over that one doubled, and place a large sterile cloth decently made, or a single piece of gauze along the length of the jaw; and tie this above according to what seems appropriate for the binding and what is convenient for the application, until it is not destroyed.
And command the patient to use rest and tranquility, and stop the food that is harmful to them.
