And then put your right hand on the uppermost part of the foot, and your left hand on the lower part of the foot at the location of the ankle.
And then put the foot on your right hand, and hold it with your left for two supports, and stretch it with your left; and press the sole of the foot against your right leg near the thigh's work.
And make two supports as we have described.
And then press the sole of the foot to the leg for the third support, and you are at the calf.
Then if it returns in one support or in two according to this method, and if you bend the foot backwards, it's good; and if not, then repeat the operation on the other side, for that which returns.
But if the reduction of the limb to what we have recommended is prohibited for you, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and stretch a piece of cloth firmly held on the ground, and which goes between their thighs, and you have wrapped around them with a sheet so that it doesn't hurt the patient.
And then one minister holds their thighs, and another minister stretches the foot with their hands or with a bandage that lies on the heel of the foot; and each minister resists against the stretching of their part, and the piece of cloth is stretched between the patient's thighs, retaining it, so that the body of the patient is not pulled towards the parts above their extension.
And then the doctor should adjust the dislocation with the healthy thighs, and another assistant should hold the sound hip to the patient's sides, so that the dislocation returns to its proper place.
And so when the dislocation returns and the health of the reduction is declared to you, then pause to apply a plaster and strongly tighten that limb with a bandage, and tie the foot to the leg with a bandage.
And beware that you protect yourself from the nerves which are behind the heel, so that the bandage on it is not violent and does not press too strongly.
And then leave it like that for two days or for three; and if the bandage is loosened, tighten it again.
And then undo it on the third day or on the fourth, and forbid the patient from moving for forty days. But if it is forgotten to put in that space, it is not done securely so that the dislocation is not dissolved and corrupted on it, and then it does not receive treatment.
And if a hot abscess occurs to it, then beware that you administer in the reduction of it what we previously mentioned, in another place of treatment and of application, until it is reduced.
Chapter Four.
On the treatment of dislocation of the toes of the feet.
It is advisable that one who is dislocated should be treated with little extension of the limb; and this which is not difficult, is easier.
More often if the dislocation is in some toes of the foot, then it is advisable to make the patient put their foot on the ground or on a table, and let them stand still as if they were walking.
And then put your foot on the ground, and place the patient's foot on what seems to be the lowest point of the joints, and then press with your foot on theirs in a downward motion so that it returns, and you will see that it has been properly realigned and does not appear out of place.
And then place the belly of their foot on a board that encloses the whole foot, which has two ends, and tighten it with a structure that is decent and firm for three days; and then undo it and make them rest from walking for many days, until it is strengthened and the recovery is assured.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
On the species of dislocation that are made with a wound or with a fracture or with whatever happens at the same time.
When accidents occur due to those things, and you perforate in the treatment of it and in the restoration of them, many witnessed successes follow, but death often occurs.
And for that it is not proper to presume on the treatment of it, except for one who is wise in the art, with long usage, merciful and pitied, slow, not hasty nor presumptuous; and who uses in the commencement of medicines that cause abscesses to heal solely, and lifts the sickness to divine judgment, but rather to the one for whom you hope for salvation from loss, and from the illness alleviation, and in which appears some hope. And therefore exert yourself so much to make the reduction in the commencement of the cause, provided that an abscess does not come to a head or burst.
And therefore if the member returns as we wish, then administer treatment which will cause the abscess to heal and cure the wound with what is convenient for it from the ointments of dried plasters.
And if it is a dislocation with a fracture and accidents occur in the separated bones, then you perforate their joint, and do to it what we have said about simple illnesses of this type that are treated in the places of those.
And beware and shun the intestine's path according to your ability in the ways of fear as my preaching has preceded you; for this is better for you to serve your Creator, and more permanent to your glory, and more salutations to your body truly those in your time.
